Important News

The Guangdong-Guangxi Armies Invade Hunan

Guangzhou dispatch: Rumors of the Guangdong and Guangxi armies intending to invade Hunan have been circulating for a long time. As of the first of this month, the armies of the two provinces finally issued a general mobilization order. The Fourth Army Group of Guangxi Province was designated as the vanguard. The 30th Regiment of Wu Qiwei, and the 34th Regiment of Shen Youcheng, both under the 12th Division of the Fourth Army, commanded by Han Hanying, deputy division commander, advanced into Qiyang at 5 PM on the first. After the Ou and Shen regiments arrived at Qiyang, Wu Qiwei personally led the 36th Regiment of Wang Weicheng, the Special Service Battalion of Wen Xiang, the Machine Gun Battalion of Liu Dingwu, and the newly formed battalion of Yin Chengwu, continuing to advance on the third. The 7th Army of Liao Lei advanced from Yongzhou and stationed in Xinning, establishing contact with the First Army Group entering Hunan from Guangdong. The 24th Division of Qin Lianfang continued to set off for Qiyang on the third, to join up with Wu Qiwei's forces. This time, Li Zongren's Fourth Army Group of Guangxi Province is entirely under the command of Bai Chongxi. As for Guangdong Province, Chen Jitang's First Army Group, since its mobilization on the first, its vanguard troops are the newly formed 5th Independent Brigade under Chen Tiejian, which entered Hunan from Pingshi on the first, and advanced to Chenxian on the second. At the same time, the 3rd Army of Li Yangjing, stationed around Lechang, also advanced towards the Hunan border. The 7th Division of Huang Yanzhen had already passed Jiufeng, and the 8th Division of Huang Zhiwen also advanced from Shao towards Lechang on the second, encamping in Lechang on the evening of the third, and advancing towards the Hunan border the next morning. The 2nd Training Regiment of the 3rd Army, under Deng Hui, traveled by military train from Maba to Shao on the second, and then to Lechang Pingshi. After the 3rd Army departed, the 1st Army of Yu Hanmou followed closely behind. The 1st Army was stationed in the northwest suburbs and around Huaxian. On the evening of the second, the headquarters prepared three special trains, departing from Huangsha to Jiangcun Dalong Letong Xinjie stations, to transport the 2nd Division of the 1st Army, under Ye Zhao, north. The 4th Regiment of Ye Gengchang and the 5th Regiment of Li Chongguang of this division arrived in Shao in batches by special train on the fourth and concentrated there. The 6th Regiment of Huang Zhinan and the Directly Subordinate Training Regiment of Deng Changqi boarded four special trains at Guotang Jiangcun on the fifth and continued to advance towards Shaoguan. It is planned that the 1st Army can be fully transported by the eleventh of this month. The Transportation Headquarters has been assigning the various armies to the No. 1, 2, 3, and 4 sub-stations in recent days. Yesterday, thirty long-distance buses were requisitioned in the province and sent to Shaole for use. Even the fertilizer-carrying troops in Guangzhou were requisitioned. (September 6)

Changsha dispatch: The Guangdong-Guangxi armies' invasion of Hunan has evolved from rumors into reality. Tang Shengzhi's forces under Yan Bogang and Chen Tiejian had already entered Hunan on the 31st of last month. The Guangdong army under Li Yangjing and others also followed closely behind. At the same time, the Guangxi army under Bai Chongxi also mobilized on the 4th of this month, reportedly to join Tang and Li's forces to advance in attack. He Jian returned to the province from Anxiang to inspect the disaster situation on the evening of the 4th. On the 6th, Gu Zhutong, the division commander of the Central Garrison Army, Liu Wendao, the director of the Hubei Civil Affairs Department, Lin Wenwei, the chief of the General Headquarters' Staff Office, and Qiu Wei, the director of the Transportation Department, arrived in Hunan. They immediately held a military conference at the General Headquarters. Gu Zhutong first reported that the Central Government had dispatched elite troops to Hunan to assist in defense, and also dispatched more than one hundred trucks to Hunan to transport troops. Subsequently, they discussed and decided on various military plans for one or two hours. It is rumored that Gu Zhutong may go to Hengzhou to inspect the defenses when necessary. (September 9)

Zhu-Mao Main Force Completely Collapses

The 19th Route Army Engages in Bloody Battles with Red Bandits

Killing Thousands of Bandits, Seizing Thousands of Guns

Nanchang dispatch: The main forces of Zhu De, Mao Zedong, Peng Dehuai, and Huang Gonglue, the false 3rd, 4th, 5th, 8th, and 12th armies, after fleeing to Xingguo, immediately established the false central government at Bailuwei and the false rear hospital in the mountains around Lizengkeng Shangzaobai. The northwest of Xingguo, Taihe, and Wan'an, the southeast of Ganxian and Yudu, and the northeast of Gaoxingwei, Chongxianwei, Shijia Yaotou, and Shacun became the central area of the Red Bandits. In mid-last month, the 19th Route Army under Chen Mingshu, together with Jiang Dingwen's forces, about four or five divisions, totaling 60,000 men, advanced west from Xingguo. At the same time, the Gong and Luo divisions were deployed along the Gan River in Taihe and Wan'an, setting up machine guns and artillery, holding the strategic passes to prevent them from escaping. However, since the armies began their operations, the Red Bandits used banditized civilians as wings and treacherous mountains as shields, evading the substantial and attacking the insubstantial, thus achieving little effect. Recently, the bandits, taking advantage of the government troops' dispersal for search and the continuous rain that made it difficult for aircraft to scout and bomb, concentrated the false 3rd Army of Huang Gonglue, the 4th Army of Lin Biao, the 5th Army of Peng Dehuai, the 12th Army of Luo Binghui, and the 35th Army of Yang Yuebin, about 70,000 to 80,000 men, with 40,000 to 50,000 guns, and fiercely attacked the 60th Division and the 9th Division of the government army northwest of Xingguo. Since the evening of the 7th, they launched more than ten assaults, with extreme ferocity. At that time, the Cai and Jiang divisions of the 19th Route Army calmly fought back without flinching. When the Red Bandits ran out of ammunition and energy, they launched a large-scale counterattack, with machine guns and artillery as dense as firecrackers. It is estimated that 6,000 to 7,000 bandits were killed. The bandits, also suffering excessive casualties, began to collapse. The government army took advantage of the victory to pursue, seizing more than 4,000 guns, four machine guns, and three mortars. At the same time, Jiang Dingwen's forces also encountered the bandit's false 3rd and 4th armies near Baiyang, and both sides engaged in close combat, which was extremely fierce. About 7,000 to 8,000 bandits and regular soldiers fell. Jiang's forces also suffered some casualties due to launching seven or eight assaults on the bandits. As for the bandits who fled south from Ningdu, they were also defeated by the 19th Route Army, which completely occupied Wangwuqian. Chen Mingshu sent a telegram to the province yesterday, briefly stating that from Yu to Jia, he had fought fiercely with Zhu De's main force of about 40,000 to 50,000 men in Gaoxing Chongxian for two days and nights. Fortunately, the soldiers fought bravely and finally defeated the bandits. The corpses of the bandits were all over the mountains and valleys, and the blood flowed into the streams, staining the plants and trees red, which was indeed a great victory since the suppression of the bandits. The bandits fleeing west have no more strength to fight, etc. After the headquarters received Chen's telegram, it immediately announced the victory and ordered Chen to continue to lead his troops to wipe out the remaining bandits to prevent future trouble. Moreover, Donggu is currently guarded by Li Yunheng's division. Li believes that the terrain of Donggu is treacherous, and it is extremely difficult to defend against the remaining bandits in the nearby mountains. Li firmly cleared the fields and defended the strategic passes, and in order to eradicate the roots of the bandits, he burned all the forests and bandit lairs, so that the bandits had nowhere to hide. Now that the bandits' bases are completely lost, even if they flee everywhere, it will not be difficult to eliminate them. (September 10)

The Flood Situation in Jiangbei Continues to Worsen

Breaches Difficult to Block

The Number of Disaster Victims Increases Daily

Yangzhou dispatch: The flooded area in Jiangbei this time spans as many as a dozen counties. Although the administrative authorities have repeatedly planned to deal with the breaches, no immediate method of blocking them has been found to date, half a month later. The number of disaster victims is increasing daily, and the relief funds raised are far from meeting the demand. The autumn wind is growing stronger, epidemics are breeding, and bandits are rising up. The current situation is worrying, and it is truly unknown how to properly resolve the aftermath. Here is a record of the dangerous situations in recent days:

In recent days, the river tides have reached their peak, and the Yi River continues to pour in. The breaches cannot be blocked immediately, resulting in daily submersion and irreparable damage. The affected areas include Xinghua, Dongtai, Yancheng, Funing, and Taixian, as well as Jiangdu and Gaoyou, which bear the brunt of the dike collapse, and the eastern parts of Baoying, Huai'an, and Huaiyin, and the counties along the river such as Yizheng and Liuhe. In recent days, the number of disaster victims transported to Yangzhou from various places has been increasing. Yangzhou, a small city also affected by the disaster, is facing increasing financial difficulties. Therefore, in the past three days, most of the disaster relief boats heading south from the north have been transferred across the river and dispatched to Zhenjiang, Nanjing, and the Su-Chang-Hu area.

Since the breach in the Grand Canal, the water that used to flow south from the north has been transformed into water flowing south from the north below Gaoyou. In recent days, the river tides have pushed the river water inward, directly pouring into the canal, and the Yi River has been rushing straight south like ten thousand horses galloping. The two rivers pass through the twenty-plus breaches in Jiang and Gao counties (a total of twenty-seven breaches, several of which were previously blocked by the Provincial Security Office), and flow east along the gaps, causing the water level in the two counties of Xing and Dong to be level with the city walls. Hundreds of miles around are without a single intact piece of land. Even coffins that have been buried can float on the surface of the water. The ferocity of the water can be seen. As for the water in Gaobao Lake, it is rapidly drying up due to the rapid outflow. Ships passing through the lake often run aground. If the breaches in the eastern dike are blocked immediately, the aquatic products in the lake within a radius of hundreds of miles next year, and the irrigation of the fields along the canal that have not been flooded, will also be sacrificed.

After a great flood, there must be a great epidemic. This has been an unchanging rule for thousands of years. Recently, the autumn wind has been growing stronger, and the disaster victims who have just emerged from the water cannot eat on time and have no fixed place to live. How can they resist external evils? Therefore, many epidemics have been discovered in the various shelters in recent days, mostly vomiting, diarrhea, fever, and chills. At present, in addition to providing food and clothing, there is an urgent need to organize clinics to provide medical treatment. (September 12)

Jiangsu Provincial Government Orders Counties to Protect the Eastern Dam

The History of the Construction of the Eastern Dam

The Eastern Dam, located in Gaochun County, is related to the water conservancy of the four prefectures of Jiangnan: Su, Song, Chang, and Tai. The Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Department of Civil Affairs recently received telegrams from Liyang, Wuxian, and other counties, stating that they had heard that the people of Chun were experiencing floodwaters from Anhui and had the intention of opening the Eastern Dam to discharge water eastward. They urgently requested that the counties be ordered to protect the dam. After receiving the telegrams, Chairman Ye immediately instructed Hu, the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, to send telegrams to the two counties of Chun and Li, ordering them to jointly and closely protect the dam and prevent unruly people from privately digging and releasing water, which would harm the entire province. At the same time, the Security Office was informed to dispatch teams to assist in the defense. As for the issue of water discharge, Jiang Fuqin was commissioned by the department to travel to Gaochun to jointly inspect an appropriate waterway with local officials and gentry and to plan another construction method for discharging the accumulated water in the county, so as to take care of both parties.

The Eastern Dam is located 120 li west of Liyang County and 60 li southeast of Gaochun County, within the territory of Gaochun County. There are two dams, upper and lower, 10 li apart. The upper dam is called the Eastern Dam, and the lower dam is called the Lower Dam. Both are built in the Xu Creek between Gucheng Town and Dengbu. The west of the Lower Dam is called the Upper River, the area between the two dams is called the Middle River, and the east of the Lower Dam is called the Lower River. The Lower River connects Liyang and Yixing in the east and flows into Tai Lake, which is the old course of the Middle River. It is said that this place originally belonged to the boundary mountains between Jiangsu and Anhui and the foothills of Maoshan Mountain, so the terrain within three to five li nearby is quite elevated. During the Spring and Autumn period, the King of Wu attacked Chu and used Wu Zixu's plan to open a river to transport grain, which was then called Xu Creek. Since then, the rivers have been connected, connecting Liangzhe in the southeast and entering the Yangtze River in the west, allowing ships to travel unimpeded. Later, the riverbed gradually silted up. It is also said that the territory of Ning, Xuan, and Guang in Anhui Province is high, and although Gaochun is relatively flat, it is still far above Liyang. When rain accumulates slightly, the mountain sources boil angrily and rush eastward. During long droughts, the source is insufficient, and ships have difficulty passing. Therefore, in the third year of Jingfu in the Tang Dynasty, Yang Xingmi built the Luyang Five Dams between the Eastern Dam and Dengbu to raise the water level in the river when the water was low, so as to facilitate navigation. During the Song Dynasty, the Five Dams gradually fell into disuse, and the water in Gaochun was easily discharged. Many people reclaimed the lakes of Shibai Gucheng as fields. The three prefectures of Su, Chang, and Hu, which were downstream, suffered particularly severe floods. Shan E and Su Shi both advocated building the Five Dams to prevent the water from Xuan, Xin, Jinling, Jiuyang, and the Yangtze River from entering Jingxi and Tai Lake, so that the water in Su and Chang could be reduced by seventy to eighty percent. At that time, the court was planning to develop the lakes and reclaim land, so it was not implemented. During the Yuan Dynasty, the rivers gradually became blocked. In the twenty-fifth year of Hongwu in the Ming Dynasty, the Xu Creek River was dredged again, and a stone gate was built to open and close, called Guangtong Town. At that time, the stone gate allowed the water from the lakes to be easily discharged, and a river was opened in the lake to divert the water from the lake and join the Qinhuai River into the Yangtze River. Thus, Su and Zhejiang went directly to Jinling via the Eastern Dam as a waterway. In the first year of Yongle in the Ming Dynasty (1403 AD), the capital was moved to the north, and the waterway was abandoned. Wu Xiang of Su cited Shan E's memorial, arguing that the water was a problem for Su and Chang, and rebuilt the earthen dam, which was the beginning of the construction of the Eastern Dam. However, the dam was still low and thin. In the sixth year of Zhengtong in the Ming Dynasty, the river water flooded, and the dam broke, causing great damage to Su and Chang. The national tax could not be collected, so it was rebuilt and strictly prohibited from releasing water. In the seventh year of Zhengde, it was increased by three zhang. In the thirty-fifth year of Jiajing (1556 AD), Japanese pirates invaded, and merchants traveled through the dam in an endless stream. The residents along the dam benefited from their exploitation and rebuilt another dam about ten li east of the Eastern Dam. The two dams were separated, and the lake water never flowed east again. Later, in the twenty-ninth year of Daoguang in the Qing Dynasty (1849 AD), there was a great flood in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River in the summer. On the twenty-sixth day of the fifth month, the villagers of Gaochun dug the Eastern Dam, and the prefectures of Su, Song, Chang, and Zhen became a vast expanse of water. An earthen dam was hastily built in July, and a stone dam was built in November, which was completed in April of the following year, costing 18,000 taels of silver. Yellow earth, lime, and sand were mixed and pounded together in the stone wall, mixed with glutinous rice juice, called three-in-one soil, to fill it, which was very solid and strong. It was also strictly forbidden to encroach on the dam foundation. Within twelve zhang north and south, it was never allowed to build houses or sheds. In the seventh year of the Republic of China, the Liyang Water Conservancy Bureau submitted a request to the Jiangnan Water Conservancy Bureau, which forwarded it to the Jiangsu Provincial Governor, to allocate funds from the mu tax to repair the dam. In the sixteenth year, workers were hired to repair the two dams and replace the side stones of the upper dam, costing a total of 20,000 yuan. The old encroachments and sheds were also cleared and demolished. It is still as solid as ever today.

Anhui Northern Disaster Relief Association Established

Bengbu dispatch: The Bengbu Chamber of Commerce believes that the flood in northern Anhui this time is extremely severe, and it is urgently necessary to handle the aftermath. It has initiated the Anhui Northern 21 Counties Flood Disaster Relief Committee. The general association is located in Bengbu, and branch associations are established in each county and important town. Representatives from various counties and towns have arrived in Bengbu. The inaugural meeting was held at the Chamber of Commerce at 3 PM on the 9th, attended by 50 representatives including Gao Weixuan. Chairman Wu Zhenwu first reported the significance of the meeting, and then discussed various proposals. The resolutions are as follows: (A) Emergency Relief: (1) The Fengyang County Government proposed that disaster relief in various counties in northern Anhui should be divided into labor and carried out in stages. It was resolved to leave it to the Executive Committee for reference. (2) Jiang Zijing and Li Yuqi, representatives of Bo County, proposed that a telegram be sent to overseas Chinese to request donations for disaster relief. It was resolved that the association would send a telegram in its name. (3) Li Shaowu, representative of Fengtai, proposed that the payment of principal and interest on 14 types of public bonds be postponed for use in price stabilization for disaster relief. It was resolved to pass it. (4) Xu Bai, Zheng Hao, and Hao Yimin, representatives of Shou County, proposed that the Tianjin Fang Yushan be pursued for embezzlement of Anhui salt tax principal and interest. It was resolved to pass it. (5) Xu Bai, Zheng Hao, and Hao Yimin, representatives of Shou County, proposed that disaster relief shelters be established in various counties. It was resolved that the association would notify the counties to consider and implement it. (6) Zhou Yushan, Xia Yuqi, and Gao Xueping, representatives of Su County, proposed that rent be extracted to assist in disaster relief. It was resolved that the association would notify the counties to handle it according to the situation. (7) The representatives of Su County also proposed that the provincial government be requested to provide loans to assist in disaster relief, to be repaid in good years. It was resolved to pass it. (8) They also proposed that the central government be requested to allocate 170,000 yuan for disaster relief in Anhui. It was resolved to pass it, and to handle it together with the 150,000 yuan in Anhui disaster relief funds deposited with the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association. (9) They also proposed that the representatives attending the meeting should voluntarily donate relief funds. It was resolved to pass it. (10) They also proposed that relief funds be solicited from wealthy households in the 21 counties, prominent overseas officials, and domestic churches. It was resolved to pass it. (11) Zhu Shaoting of Fengyang County suggested that reed mats be purchased and porridge factories be established for relief. It was resolved to pass it. (B) Work Relief and River Guidance: (12) Wang Yixian, representative of Fengyang, proposed that the government be requested to advance the guidance of the Huai River for work relief. It was resolved to pass it. (13) Li Shaowu, representative of Fengtai, proposed that the National Government's Huai River Guidance Committee implement the guidance of the Huai River in the shortest possible time for work relief. It was resolved to pass it. (14) Ban Fu of Fengyang County proposed that the dikes of the Huai River be repaired in the spring and winter after they collapse. It was resolved to pass it. (15) The Bengbu Chamber of Commerce proposed that the Feih River be dredged for work relief. It was resolved to pass it. (16) It also proposed that the Ministry of Railways be requested to increase the number of bridge holes or find other remedies in the flooded areas of Huaibei. It was resolved to pass it. (17) Huang Shili and Huang Weizhai, representatives of Chu County, proposed that the unused road construction funds in northern Anhui be used for dike repair. It was resolved to pass it. (18) Chen Ziheng, representative of Fengyang, proposed a plan to rescue disaster victims with food, clothing, and shelter. The original plan was passed. (C) Request for Exemption from Land Tax: (19) Jiang Yizhai and Jiang Zhongwen, representatives of Quanjiao, proposed that the autumn land tax for this year be exempted. It was resolved to pass it. (D) Case of Weitian Surcharge: (20) Jiang Zijing and Li Yuqi, representatives of Bo County, proposed that the payment of Weitian be postponed. It was resolved to pass it. (E) Regarding Transportation: (21) Ji Shaowu, representative of Fengtai, proposed that ways be found to maintain transportation along the Huai River. The original plan was passed. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Anhui Province Requests Additional Emergency Relief

Request for Additional Allocation of 100,000 Due to the Severity of the Disaster

The flood in Anhui Province is extremely severe, followed by a hurricane, which has further expanded the disaster area. The 170,000 yuan in relief funds previously allocated by the central government has been exhausted. Chen Diaoyuan, chairman of the provincial government, learned that Yan Zhuang, a member of the Central Relief Committee, was about to go to Jiangxi, and specially convened a meeting of all members of the Provincial Relief Committee to discuss the distribution of emergency relief. The previous distribution covered 16 counties in the first-level disaster area, with 15,000 yuan allocated to each of the nine counties including Huaining, and 5,000 yuan to Linhuai. The remaining seven counties had not yet been distributed. He and the Yan Committee telegraphed the Disaster Relief Committee of the Executive Yuan, requesting additional relief funds. Excerpts from the telegram are as follows: (1) The central government allocated 170,000 yuan for emergency relief in Anhui Province. Jing Yuan carried it to Anhui, and according to the disaster situation in various places, it was decided to allocate 4,700 yuan to each of the nine counties of Huaining, Tongcheng, Wangjiang, Dongliu, Tongling, Wuhu, Shouxian, Huoqiu, and Wuhe, and 2,000 yuan for emergency rescue of the moat embankment in the provincial capital. The deficit was supplemented by the provincial government, and the relief methods for each county were determined to rescue the destitute elderly and weak, with each person receiving at least about one yuan in relief funds. The distribution of silver, the distribution of flour, or the establishment of factories to distribute porridge were the three methods. The county governments, together with the county party departments and county disaster relief organizations, weighed the local situation and chose one to implement. However, after the great flood in Anhui Province, the disaster area has been further expanded and the disaster situation has become more severe due to the hurricane. Moreover, the relief funds in the affected areas are often unable to provide universal relief, which seems to be partial and withered. A telegram has been sent to the Disaster Relief Committee of the National Government, requesting an additional 100,000 yuan for emergency relief, to be remitted to Anhui for distribution. (2)

The flood was already extremely severe. According to reports from various counties, nearly 30 counties are classified as first-level and second-level disaster areas. However, Heaven did not tire of inflicting disaster. On the 25th of last month, another hurricane struck, further expanding the disaster area and making the damage even more severe. The 170,000 yuan in emergency relief from the central government has been allocated to the nine counties of Huaining, Tongcheng, Wangjiang, Dongliu, Tongling, Wuhu, Shouxian, Huoqiu, and Wuhe, with 15,000 yuan each, 5,000 yuan to Linhuai in Fengyang, and 4,700 yuan each to the six counties of Wuwei, He County, Xuancheng, Guichi, Fengtai, and Huaiyuan. In addition, 2,000 yuan was allocated for the emergency rescue of the moat embankment in the provincial capital, and the deficit was supplemented by the provincial government. However, the disaster is severe and the funds are limited. Even the disaster areas with the same situation cannot be universally relieved, which seems to be partial and withered. Please quickly allocate an additional 100,000 yuan for emergency relief, to be remitted to Anhui by a certain date for distribution. (September 12)

Ge Guangting's Conversation After Returning to Qingdao

There Is No Need to Worry About the Security of North China

The Clearing of the Countryside in Lu-Yu Is About to Begin

Qingdao dispatch: Ge Guangting, chairman of the Jiaojiao Railway Committee, recently went to Peiping to visit Deputy Commander Zhang, and reported on everything. After finishing his business, he returned to Jinan with Chairman Han, and then accompanied him on a trip to Henan. He returned to Qingdao from Jinan at 7:30 this morning (the 10th). I visited him in the afternoon. According to Ge, Deputy Commander Zhang's health has been improving day by day recently, and he has been receiving guests and working as usual. He will be discharged from the hospital soon. Because the security of North China is important, it has been decided that he will stay in Peiping and will not go anywhere else in the near future. The proposal to return to Liaoning has been cancelled. Regarding the security issue of North China, Deputy Commander Zhang has consulted with generals from all parties several times. The generals all believe that at this time of floods and national crisis, the country cannot afford to start another war. Therefore, no matter what, they are determined to uphold the principle of peace. After this consultation, the security of North China can be consolidated without worry. Chairman Han met with Deputy Commander Zhang several times after arriving in Peiping, and both sides were very happy. I (Ge refers to himself) and Chairman Han are old colleagues, so Deputy Commander Zhang asked me to be the representative in Jinan to facilitate communication. After returning to Jinan with Chairman Han from Peiping, I originally planned to return to Qingdao immediately, but Chairman Han insisted on inviting me to Henan, so I stayed for a few more days. Regarding the clearing of the countryside in Lu-Yu, Chairman Han and Chairman Liu (Zhi) have consulted several times. The clearing methods have been decided and will be implemented soon. As for Yan Xishan, he must go abroad sooner or later. The generals of the Jin army have expressed their firm intention that no matter what, they cannot disrupt the overall situation for personal reasons. Deputy Commander Zhang also believes that if Yan does not leave Shanxi Province for a day, the people will not be at ease for a day. He will urge Yan together with the generals to leave Shanxi as soon as possible, etc. After the conversation, I took my leave. (September 10)

▲ Wuhu's water level rose significantly again last night, surpassing previous record highs. The elevated planks used for passage were once again submerged, hindering transportation. The Flood Relief Association hosted reporters from various newspapers, with County Magistrate Yu reporting on the Wuhu disaster situation, which differs from other areas. Because more than ten counties inland have accumulated water that must exit through Wuhu, and the river tide is not receding, the water level in Wuhu will take some time to drop. The disaster situation may worsen. Currently, Huangchi has received over 20,000 refugees, and Wuhu has been receiving over a thousand people daily, along with more farmers and cattle. The Flood Relief Association has expedited the establishment of shelters, with He Wuzi and others in charge.

▲ Zhang Gongheng, the Central Government's disaster investigation commissioner, along with representatives from the Wuhu Flood Relief Association and the Nanfan Five Counties Flood Relief Charity Association, hired a special boat at 7:00 AM today to investigate the disaster situation in counties such as Fanchang and Nanling.

The Anhui Provincial Government, considering the rampant banditry along the river in various counties in recent years, which endangers merchants and travelers, specifically ordered the counties to jointly develop joint defense measures. Yesterday at 9:00 AM, representatives from the county governments of Chaoxian, Guichi, Dangtu, Huaining, and Wangjiang, as well as the Provincial Ship Management Office, the Wuhu Shipping Association, and the Datong Public Security Bureau, gathered at the Wuhu County Government to hold a waterborne joint defense conference. County Magistrate Yu Yuying of Wuhu presided over the meeting, reading out the proposals from various counties. A resolution was passed outlining four main areas: joint defense, patrol and investigation, search and suppression, and investigation. It was decided to continue the meeting at 1:00 PM today to determine the implementation methods for the joint defense area.

▲ The export of Wuhu rapeseed, previously resolved through meetings by various sectors, was permitted for shipments to Shanghai. However, yesterday, the Anti-Japanese Association again detained and refused to release the shipments. The Grain Joint Association believes this violates the resolutions of various sectors and affects commerce and workers' livelihoods. They have submitted another request to the Public Security Bureau and the Party Rectification Committee, asking them to order the Anti-Japanese Association not to obstruct rapeseed exports on ships other than Japanese vessels, to avoid causing disputes.

▲ To raise police funding, the Public Security Bureau convened a meeting at 2:00 PM today at the County Chamber of Commerce, gathering gentry, wealthy individuals, and representatives from various businesses. It was resolved to transform the previously established Public Security Maintenance Association into a temporary Public Security Maintenance Association. Fifteen executive committee members, five standing committee members, and seven supervisory committee members were elected on the spot. Funding will be collectively raised by all members. Letter from the Ministry of Interior

To the Editor: Previously, your newspaper's advertisement section on July 3rd carried an advertisement for the Production and Consumption Survey Institute's recruitment, which included a solemn statement: "On June 7th, Wang Pixian, a fellow villager who studied in Japan, and the Production and Consumption Survey Institute of the Ministry of Interior, appointed me as a physical examination committee member," Upon reading this, I was shocked. This Ministry does not have a Production and Consumption Survey Institute. The fact that Wang Pixian dared to use its name to attempt fraud is illegal. As this concerns the reputation of the Ministry, we have consulted the Shanghai Municipal Government for investigation. It replied that it had dispatched officers to investigate. Yin Muqi claimed that Wang Pixian was from Changzhou and a former classmate who studied in Japan. He was staying at the Jiuhua Hotel in Shanghai. However, by the time the police arrived at the hotel, he was no longer there. In addition to ordering a continued investigation to apprehend him, we have replied to your newspaper for verification and publication in the letters section, so that the public may know the truth. Sincerely, Ministry of Interior, September 11th.

Special Publication

Flood Disaster and Future Chinese Water Conservancy Problems

Shen Yi

Post-flood relief is certainly important, but the most crucial element remains a long period of peace within the country. Strictly speaking, this flood is purely a result of the internal strife of the past twenty years and is not an accidental event. Readers, consider: if there had been no internal strife, how could water conservancy projects across the country have fallen into such disrepair? If water conservancy projects had not been so neglected, even in the face of a flood, how could we have been so helpless this time? To be a nation in the 20th century and still suffer floods every year is a rare occurrence in the world. Our country, still claiming to be a civilized nation, must consider how to wash away this shame.

I once vowed to study historical materials on the Yellow River and compile a chronology to clarify the traces of its governance and chaos. In doing so, I read various local gazettes and old Chinese water conservancy books and came across a very interesting fact: the rise and fall of water conservancy is, in reality, mutually causal with the governance and chaos of successive dynasties. For example, during the Tang Dynasty's 288 years, there were 32 Yellow River disasters, averaging one every nine years. In the Yuan Dynasty's 108 years, there were 91 Yellow River disasters, averaging more than one per year. Even without comparing the politics of the Tang and Yuan dynasties in other aspects, this alone can give us a general idea. In a peaceful country, the authorities have the spare capacity to attend to water conservancy, and water conservancy flourishes. Otherwise, with constant disturbances, even if they have the intention, they lack the power. From this perspective, can the frequency of floods since the founding of the Republic be said not to be due to internal strife? Therefore, to eliminate floods, one must seek long-term peace for the country, so that construction projects can proceed in an orderly manner. If this is the case, and water conservancy does not flourish, and floods continue to occur as they do today, who would believe it?

Although the government could not prevent this flood beforehand, it must make efforts to remedy it afterward. And the so-called post-disaster remedy is not just temporary disaster relief but the prevention of future disasters. In the autocratic era of the past, when a major flood occurred, the monarch could not avoid issuing a decree of self-reproach. Although this was somewhat staged, it could not be said not to be a kind of expression of responsibility. Local officials at the time would personally pray to Heaven for divine assistance. Although the practice was foolish, it was nonetheless an expression of responsibility. This kind of expression is certainly not worth emulating, nor is it something to be discussed today. However, the government must take responsibility for the occurrence of such events and their aftermath. There is no difference between the past and the present. Today's government expresses its responsibility for the flood by striving to prevent future floods, in addition to disaster relief. The way to prevent future floods is nothing other than the construction and repair of water conservancy projects in peacetime. As the saying goes, "The overturned cart ahead is a warning to the cart behind," and "The past cannot be追, but the future can still be caught up with." This is what it means.

According to newspaper reports, this flood was most severe in the Yangtze River basin, followed by the area north of the Yangtze, where the flooding was also significant. The Yangtze River has always been known as a river that brings benefits and not harm. However, judging from recent conditions, this is far from the case. Taking the section from Hankou to Wusong as an example, every winter and spring, the water level becomes shallow due to siltation. Ships with a slightly deeper draft can often only reach Wuhu. Above Wuhu, goods must be transferred to barges. The depth of the problem is not something that has occurred overnight. As for the major flooding in Wuhan this time, it is even more shocking. The reasons for this are nothing more than the failure to maintain water conservancy projects in recent years, the increasing siltation of the mainstreams and tributaries, and the encroachment of private individuals on the islands and sandbars in the water storage areas of various lakes, leaving no room for the water, which then bursts its banks and causes disaster. In addition, the amount and area of rainfall in various places during July and August this year were unusually high. The upstream areas also lacked forests and appropriate engineering works. The water rushed down rapidly, causing flooding that was impossible to resist. The three towns of Wuhan, located at the confluence of the Yangtze and Han Rivers, experienced simultaneous rises in the mainstreams and tributaries. Even if the dikes were very solid, it is feared that under such circumstances, the floodwaters could still overflow the dikes. Moreover, the dikes themselves were originally very weak. The middle reaches of the Yangtze River have many lakes, such as Dongting Lake and Poyang Lake. Normally, the lake surfaces are vast, and the rivers run crisscross. Whenever the Yangtze River is in high flood, the water is stored in the lakes, which reduces the force of the flood. When the water recedes, the stored water is gradually discharged, so that the water source does not dry up. Therefore, the increase and decrease in its water volume changes with the rise and fall of the Yangtze River. It is nothing less than a natural reservoir for the Yangtze River. In the past, the Yangtze River was able to avoid flooding mainly for this reason. Unfortunately, since the late Qing Dynasty, various provinces have established sand field bureaus that have indiscriminately sold water lands without regard to the impact on waterways. Their work was not aligned with water conservancy agencies, and their goals were completely contradictory. In such a situation, it would be truly rare for floods not to occur. The management of water, like the treatment of illness, requires careful examination and cannot be based on guesswork. Therefore, how to manage the Yangtze River in the future cannot be decided by a few words right now. However, speaking in principle, the Yangtze River itself and all its tributaries must be dredged separately. The dikes along the Yangtze River must be repaired and protected separately. The original functions of the various lakes that store water must be restored. In other words, the encroached lands, regardless of whether they were legally obtained, should all be returned to the water if they conflict with the management plan. In addition, the affairs of the sand field bureaus should be transferred to the competent water conservancy agencies to ensure that the work is not contradictory. The latter is not only true for the management of the Yangtze River, but it is also necessary to find ways to correct this situation in any place where it exists. After the occurrence of this flood, someone mentioned a saying of Mr. Zhang Jian from the past, which meant that if the Huai River was not properly diverted, Wuhan would inevitably be submerged one day. Unfortunately, today his words have come true, which cannot be said not to be a coincidence. As a result, there are sighs about the fact that the Huai River was not tamed and managed earlier. Some people also believe that the proposal to divert the Huai River has been advocated for a long time, and the disputes over whether it should enter the Yangtze River or the sea have not been resolved in a single day. If the plan recently set by the Huai River Diversion Committee is followed, it will focus on entering the Yangtze River. Now that the Yangtze River is suffering from flooding, if the Huai River is added to it, would it not be even worse? Therefore, from the experience of this flood, it is still possible to fully research and consider the plan before it is implemented. This may not be a great stroke of fortune. In my opinion, if Mr. Zhang Jian had said this, he would have meant diverting the Huai River into the sea. He meant that if the Huai River does not enter the sea, it will inevitably enter the Yangtze River. Once the Yangtze and Huai Rivers both rise, the Yangtze River will be pushed up by the Huai River, and its momentum will be great, so Wuhan will be in danger. However, as far as I know, this flood in Wuhan is not entirely the fault of the Huai River. If the diversion of the Huai River into the Yangtze River had already become a reality, then the flooding around Nanjing would not have been as severe as it is today, and the flood disaster in the area north of the Yangtze River would not have been as serious as it is today. This is what I dare to say. This statement may seem unreasonable at first glance, but in fact, without the diversion of the Huai River, most of its floodwaters would have no other way to be discharged except into the Yangtze River. Once it is diverted, the Hongze Lake can store part of the Huai River's floodwaters, and the diversion into the sea can divert part of them. In this way, the amount of water entering the Yangtze River during a flood can be much less than it was in the past. People today do not examine this carefully. When they hear that the Huai River Diversion Plan advocates first managing the route into the Yangtze River, they immediately think it is not possible. They do not know that even if the route into the Yangtze River is not managed, the Huai River still enters the Yangtze River every day without any restrictions. The amount entering the Yangtze River even accounts for the vast majority of the Huai River's water. The reason why the Huai River is causing disaster today is precisely this. Let us say that the diversion of the Huai River into the Yangtze River must be opposed. However, no one has paid attention to the fact that it is entering the Yangtze River without being diverted. Is this not strange? Some may say that this is why they advocate diverting the Huai River into the sea. In my opinion, diverting the Huai River into the sea is certainly possible in terms of engineering. What needs to be studied is whether it is economical and whether it is within the capacity of the country today. According to the Huai River Diversion Committee's plan, in addition to diverting the Huai River into the Yangtze River, it also considers diverting it into the sea and using the Hongze Lake to build a flood storage reservoir to limit the flow of the Huai River into the Yangtze River during a flood, so that the flood level of the Yangtze River will not be affected. If the above ideals can all be realized in fact, then this plan should not only not be shaken by this flood but should also be implemented more quickly as a result.

However, is it easy to talk about diverting the Huai River? To divert the Huai River without considering the Yellow River is equivalent to not diverting it at all. Two years ago, I wrote an article on diverting the Huai River and managing the Yellow River, which was published in various newspapers. I described the close relationship between the Yellow and Huai Rivers and the danger of the current state of the Yellow River. I believed that if one does not want to divert the Huai River today, so be it. If one wants to divert the Huai River, one must first manage the Yellow River. There is no way to seek temporary peace without managing the Yellow River. However, people in Jiangsu and Anhui have a very mistaken view, which is that the Yellow River has not had the possibility of invading the south since it moved north and diverted into the Ji River into the sea in the fifth year of Xianfeng. Ding Xian of Shanyang seems to have once made this statement. However, according to my speculation, Ding Xian was one of the most vocal advocates of diverting the Huai River. At that time, he saw the Yellow River moving north and believed that this was the only good opportunity to divert the Huai River. However, the intensity of the disaster caused by the confluence of the Yellow and Huai Rivers was still fresh in the memory of the people along the Huai River. If a way was not found to eliminate their psychological fears, the resistance to diverting the Huai River would be considerable. Therefore, he intentionally made the statement that the Yellow River would not come south again after moving north. This was probably Ding Xian's deliberate cleverness. With Ding Xian's intelligence and knowledge, how could he not know that the Yellow River's frequent invasions of the Huai River, since it could move north in the past, why could it not return south in the future? People today do not examine this and still believe it to be true, which is truly regrettable. During the Ming and Qing dynasties, when the Yellow and Huai Rivers merged, those who managed the rivers, such as Chen Xuan, Pan Jixun, Liu Daxia, and Jin Fu, either built high dikes, constructed the Taihang Dike, or created water-constricting dikes outside Yuntiguan. These people were broad-minded and had well-thought-out plans. However, once the Yellow River breached to the north, all their efforts were in vain. Therefore, even if one wants to bury one's head and talk about diverting the Huai River today, even if the Huai River is indeed diverted, how can one guarantee that the Yellow River will not invade the south? As the ancients said, "Those who manage a hundred li of a river should have their sights set on a thousand li away, and those who manage the river in front of them should calculate a hundred years into the future." This is what it means. Since the Yellow River moved north and diverted into the Ji River into the sea, the harm to the Ji River has been equal to the harm to the Huai River when it was diverted in the past. In recent years, breaches have often occurred in the Shandong area, which proves that the tail end is not smooth and has reached its limit. If this continues, the tail end will become increasingly unsmooth, and the water will have nowhere to go. Its momentum will inevitably breach its banks, and the events of Tongwaxiang in the fifth year of Xianfeng will inevitably be repeated today. I only hope that my words are not true; otherwise, the intensity of the disaster will be no less than this flood. I am not fond of making alarmist statements. The lessons of the past are all there. I cannot hide them. I simply do not understand why people throughout the country pay attention to other rivers but are so indifferent to the Yellow River. Are they going to wait for a disaster to occur before talking about management? This is truly something I cannot bear to know. Foreign experts hired to come to China, such as Freeman, Fang Xiu, and the engineering team of the American Red Cross, came for the purpose of diverting the Huai River. However, reading their reports, one can see between the lines that they all regard managing the Yellow River as more urgent than diverting the Huai River. Freeman said in his Plan for the Management of the Huai River, "The author has always regarded saving the Yellow River, the great disaster of China, as his only concern." The report on diverting the Huai River by the engineering team of the American Red Cross contains the following statement: "The Yellow and Huai Rivers may in fact be able to merge again. If so, all engineering works will be destroyed. For this reason, the engineering team believes that this report cannot be considered complete unless the relationship between the Yellow and Huai Rivers is studied in detail." Professor Fang Xiu, a German consultant to the Huai River Diversion Committee, also said in his report, "The problem that is most closely related to diverting the Huai River is the Yellow River problem. If the Yellow River breaches to the south again, the entire effort to divert the Huai River will be in vain." Alas, if the Yellow River breaches to the south, it will inevitably carry the waters of the Huai River into the Yangtze River. It will not only render the entire effort to divert the Huai River in vain but will also make the future management of the Yangtze River and all post-flood relief problems increasingly complex. What I feel is dangerous, I dare not hide it. I hope that those in the country who are concerned about water conservancy will take a look at it in addition to rushing to provide disaster relief.

The First Day of the Shanghai Municipal Games

Solemn Opening Ceremony, Male and Female Athletes Show Their Skills

Qian Hangsu's Women's Long Jump Sets a New Shanghai Record

Today's Track and Field Events Include Seventeen Finals, Tennis Begins, and Soccer and Volleyball Continue

The Shanghai Second Municipal Games, which had been heavily publicized, opened yesterday at 1:00 PM. With a clear breeze, refreshing air, and spectators gathering, the thin clouds in the sky and the proud, piercing sun were perfect for sports. The bells rang twice, signaling the completion of the opening ceremony. Track and field athletes, soccer players, and volleyball players competed in their respective fields, creating a vibrant atmosphere. The details are recorded below.

An Overview of the Venue

The opening ceremony was held at the China Track and Field Stadium. Spectators began to arrive in droves at 12:00 PM. Boy Scouts checked admission tickets at the gate, while most of the athletes had already arrived before noon, either rubbing their legs and resting in the waiting area or jogging slowly on the track to loosen their muscles. The command platform on the west side of the track was filled with prizes, including silver trophies, silk banners, mirror stands, and medals, all shining brilliantly. Guests included representatives from the Municipal Party Committee, bureau directors, Chu Minyi, Wang Xiaolai, and more than forty others. The audience surrounded the stands, with the most people on the west side, followed by the east side, and the fewest on the north side, totaling about seven or eight thousand people. The soccer field and volleyball court each had over a thousand people as well. The venue's order was maintained by Boy Scouts from various schools, distributed by the Shanghai Boy Scouts Council, and was well-organized.

Grand Parade

The opening ceremony began at 1:00 PM, starting with a parade around the track. The order was as follows: the Public Security Bureau band led the way, followed by the most important guests, staff, female athletes, and finally, male athletes bringing up the rear. Wang Zhuangfei, holding a megaphone in front, gave commands, while Huang Shengbai and Yu Jiajun, holding the Party and national flags, led the way. The large group of people proceeded in an orderly fashion, circling more than half the track, with over seven hundred people. Videographers and photographers followed closely, filming and photographing, creating a busy scene.

Opening Ceremony

After the entire group paraded from in front of the command platform back to the original location, the athletes lined up on the track. Officials, guests, and staff took their seats. Everyone stood solemnly, sang the Party song, paid respects, and finished reading the will. Then, Chairman Zhang Yuejun gave a speech, followed by a speech by the Municipal Party Committee representative, Tong Xingbai, a speech by Chu Minyi, and finally, a report by Vice Chairman Xu Peihuang. The details of each are recorded below.

▲ Chairman Zhang's Speech: "Distinguished instructors, guests, male and female athletes, the Municipal Games were held once last year in March. Now, we are holding the Second Municipal Games and, in accordance with the regulations, will select representatives for the National Games in the twentieth year of the Republic. Today is the opening day of the Games. The sky is high and the air is crisp, and the beautiful autumn light is the perfect time to try out your skills. The enthusiasm of the participants and the joy and excitement of the general audience all prove that the citizens' enthusiasm for physical education is significantly more enthusiastic than in the first Games, there has been significant progress compared to the first Games. In the future competition, there will be even more new records. This good phenomenon is very gratifying. There are three points that I, as the Chairman, still cannot refrain from mentioning:

First, we should focus on the spiritual aspect. Our national spirit has been lost for a long time. In recent years, we have been trying to save and revitalize it, and we have come to realize that to restore the national spirit, we must start by focusing on physical education. Therefore, sports meetings at the provincial and municipal levels and the National Games have been held in succession, and although they have achieved considerable results, the spiritual aspect has not yet reached a sufficient and satisfactory level. Therefore, whenever we encounter natural disasters, man-made calamities, foreign aggression, or internal strife, we cannot stop or melt them with the entire national spirit so that they will never be seen again under the blue sky and white sun. Although this sufficient and satisfactory entire national spirit cannot be achieved overnight, we must be down-to-earth and move forward step by step to achieve the final success. It is hoped that all participants will strive to be strong, show their skills, and not give up halfway in every sport, regardless of the result. They must implement their ideas and persevere to create new records, promote our national spirit, and use this spirit to save the nation, save the world, and save humanity, so that they can create a new career.

Second, we should focus on the moral aspect. Sports meetings should first focus on the spirit, but the moral aspect should not be neglected, especially the integration of the spirit into morality. In ancient China, there was archery, which emphasized courtesy and respect, with absolutely no room for deception or usurpation. Today's sports meetings have the same purpose and meaning as ancient archery. Although the nature is competitive, the purpose is still sports. Participants will inevitably have a desire to compete, but they should not harm others to benefit themselves. They should all abide by the regulations and obey orders. Any outrageous actions or immoral behavior will be rejected by the entire meeting. Moreover, attention should also be paid to maintaining order at this grand venue with so many participants. If the above is understood by everyone, the result will naturally be satisfactory.

Third, we should focus on skills. The purpose of sports meetings is to compete in skills, but if there are shortcomings in the spiritual or moral aspects, the original intention of the sports meeting will be lost. Therefore, we first emphasize the spirit, then morality, and finally skills. I hope that all participants will reflect on the situation of the last sports meeting. In the positive aspect, they should of course strive to improve on all the achievements of the last time. In the negative aspect, they should ensure that all the previous shortcomings do not happen again. Most importantly, the results of the competition will inevitably have winners and losers. The winners should not be complacent and should continue to strive for perfection to prepare for the National Games in the future and win glory for the city. Those who do not win should not be discouraged and lose heart. Failure is the mother of success, and they should continue to work hard. If their skills are truly excellent, they will naturally stand out.

All participants should pay close attention to the above three points. Furthermore, many officials and staff from various agencies under the municipal government have participated in amateur sports. Although the results cannot be predicted, this courageous spirit truly demonstrates their enthusiasm for sports. The city has high hopes for them."

Parade in Formation

Municipal Party Committee Representative Tong Xingbai's Speech: "Chairman, athletes, guests, representatives, today I am representing the Municipal Party Committee to participate in the Shanghai Second Municipal Games, and I feel very happy. Chairman Zhang has spoken in detail about the important points of the Games, so there is no need for me to elaborate. I would like to offer a few minor points: (1) Sports should be universal, not limited to a part. Usually, those who participate in competitions at sports meetings are all school students, and among the students, only a minority of the entire school participates. Those who love sports in elementary school stop in middle school, those who love sports in middle school stop when they enter university, and those who love sports in university stop when they enter the workforce. In this situation, how can the popularization of physical education be easy? I now hope that those of you who have a solid foundation in sports will develop and promote it. (2) Sports should be sustainable, not temporary. Often, many athletes work hard to practice when the sports meeting is approaching, but after the sports meeting, they put it aside lightly, so there is very little benefit to their physical fitness and spiritual cultivation. I hope that after the meeting, regardless of whether you win or lose, you will continue to practice. The above two points are well known to everyone, and I am not afraid to be verbose because I want to ask everyone to never forget them."

▲ Chu Minyi's Speech: "Chairman, instructors, athletes, guests, I have just returned from Xinjiang and am very happy to be able to attend this grand event. In this China, where natural disasters and man-made calamities are intertwined, many people want to postpone the sports meeting, and their reasons are sufficient. However, strengthening the body and promoting national spirit are essential for China today. The bodies of the average Chinese person seem to be too weak, so they lack the drive to take initiative. If the badge of "sick man" given by foreigners can find a way out through sports, transform the body, and create a healthy individual, then they can serve the Party and the country. For example, I was able to travel tens of thousands of miles to the Northwest and return safely thanks to my daily training."

Opening Ceremony

(Photo by this newspaper)

"I hope that all athletes will show their training efforts in this meeting and then go to the National Games to get a good position to show the true spirit of Shanghai."

▲ Vice Chairman Xu's Report: "Chairman, guests, staff, athletes, the purpose of this sports meeting is to promote physical education for all citizens and to select representatives for the National Games. According to statistics, the number of participants in the track and field events is 248 men and 72 women, in swimming 64 men and 9 women, in tennis 39 men and 5 women, in soccer 9 teams, in baseball 4 teams, in volleyball 4 men's teams and 6 women's teams, in basketball 11 men's teams and 3 women's teams, and in Chinese martial arts over 100 people. The distribution of championships is as follows: men have track and field, all-around, swimming, soccer, basketball, tennis, volleyball, and baseball, for a total of nine categories. Women have track and field, swimming, basketball, tennis, and volleyball, for a total of five categories. Chinese martial arts has wrestling, fencing, and pugilism for both men and women. The dates are from today to the 19th. I am deeply grateful to the officials, representatives of the Municipal Party Committee, representatives from all walks of life, sports figures, and journalists for their enthusiastic support in making this event a success. The two days after the meeting, the 19th and 20th, are the dates for the health and sports competition for municipal government officials. This move was initiated by the mayor and the heads of various bureaus to promote public sports among all citizens. The technical skills may not be very good, but the spirit is very positive."

Daxia 21 to 16 Datong

21 to 9

Datong's lack of powerful spiking, heavy hits over the net, and frequent out-of-bounds shots resulted in a large difference in scores. In the first set, Daxia won by a large margin, 21 to 11. The second set was fiercely contested, with the score reaching 15 to 14, Daxia only winning by one point. Datong could not continue to catch up and lost. In the third set, Datong was even more overwhelmed, losing 21 to 9.

Yesterday's preliminary football matches totaled two games: (1) Hua Ling eliminated Pei Lei five to one; (2) Zhi Xing eliminated Western District three to one. A brief account follows:

(1) Hua Ling Wins Against Pei Lei

Hua Ling Team Lineup

Fan Liang

This match should have been considered a forfeit by Pei Lei, as they didn't have enough players and hastily pulled people together to make up the numbers. The referee only discovered this after the match had begun. Fortunately, Hua Ling won; otherwise, there would have been another problem. As a result, Pei Lei was completely overwhelmed, under heavy pressure for the entire ninety minutes. Within five steps, there were no opposing players to be found. Hua Ling swept the field for a time. In the first fifteen minutes, Hua Ling's center forward, Jia Jiliang, scored a goal. Later, Pei Lei had a chance to counterattack, and Hua Ling's left winger, Zheng Zhirong, committed a foul. Pei Lei's center forward, Wang Kezu, kicked in a goal, making the score two to one. Hua Ling's left inside forward, Luo Douwen, received a pass from Wu Jiugao and scored, making it two to two. Pei Lei's inside defender committed a foul, and Jia Youliang scored from a penalty kick. Liu Zongde and Wu Jiugao also each scored a goal, ending the game at five to one.

(2) Zhi Xing Wins Against Western District

Three to One

Zhi Xing Team Lineup

Tu Yushi, Wan Xianghua

Huang Zonghua, Zhang Jinxiang, Gong Yibin

Lu Zhiming, Fang Chaojun

Zhi Xing was the champion of the Chinese Football Association's Chinese Character Group last year. Although some players were absent, the team still looked strong. Although Western District lost, they resisted fiercely. In the first half, Zhi Xing scored two goals, making it two to zero. The left inside forward, Wan Mian, single-handedly broke through the defense, scoring just ten minutes into the game. Then, center forward Gong Yibin hooked the ball to the left from twenty yards away from the goal, scoring a spectacular goal. In the second half, no goals were scored for twenty minutes. When Western District attacked near the goal and there was a scramble, center back Zhang Jinxiang fell and touched the ball, so Western District scored a goal with a penalty kick, bringing the score to two to one. Finally, Zhi Xing's right inside forward, Fang Chaojun, received a pass from Wan Xianghua and easily scored the fourth goal, ending the game at three to one.
