Xiexing Pharmaceutical Factory Benefits Disaster Victims

Distributing Shengdan at Reception Centers

The local Xiexing Pharmaceutical Factory is enthusiastic about charity. Previously, in view of the major floods in various parts of the country, when Mr. Xiang Songmao of the Flood Relief Association raised medicines for distribution to the disaster areas, the factory donated a box of Shengdan, totaling 12,000 packets. This was previously reported in the newspapers. Subsequently, the New Medicine Industry Association initiated a campaign from September 1st to 5th to donate 10% of the proceeds from sales in the retail departments to flood relief. At that time, Xiexing Pharmaceutical Factory, because its products such as Bailingji, Shengdan, Jiufu Milk White Cod Liver Oil, and Buliduo were mainly distributed through pharmacies and rarely sold retail, specially donated 200 yuan to help with flood relief. Recently, it was reported that many disaster victims arriving in Shanghai were suffering from illnesses due to unsuitable living and eating conditions. The factory specially sent people to carry the Shengdan it produces to Hunan Guild Hall, Qu Zhenren Temple, Chao Huishan Village Wanggong Temple, Chaozhou Guild Hall, Fire God Temple and other places for inspection and donation, totaling several thousand packets. The disaster victims were overjoyed by this, thinking that the packets they received would bring them new life. The distributors wanted to express the great efficacy of the medicine, meaning to bring the dead back to life. The disaster victims, seeing this empathy, felt a renewed sense of vitality and received a lot of comfort and hope. The local pharmaceutical industry urgently provides public health medicines and distributes them separately to help make up for the lack of equipment in public institutions and relief organizations. This will prevent many unexpected diseases among the disaster victims, which is also an essential plan for relief.

It is now learned that the store owner invited the judges to hold a judging meeting last night, and the rankings have been determined. The first prize for women was Tang Naiqi, the second prize was Wang Tonghua, the third prize was Qian Yucan, the fourth prize was Sun Yingqing, and the fifth prize was Fan Bi. The first prize for men was Xiao Yanbin, the second prize was Gu Rongzhan, the third prize was Wang Liangtong, the fourth prize was Li Yiren, the fifth prize was Yu Jingfu, and the subsequent prizes were Gan Niu, Zhang Mengzhao, You Jikai, Zhou Jintao, and Zhu Youcai. The five mixed design prizes were Liu Xuezhen, Cheng Kejian, Chen Kexian, Zhu Yue, and Zhang Jianqiu. In addition to the prizes for the first to fifth places in the women's and men's categories, those after the fifth place will also be given a piece of clothing material worth four or five yuan as a thank you.

Kicked in the Kidney and Died

Lu Jiameng's Life Ends

Lu Jiameng, 23 years old, from Yangzhou, the owner of the Liangxinyuan stove shop in Shenjiawan, Wusong Road, Zhabei, used to be a groom. The day before yesterday, he had a dispute over money with Du Wenshan, 18 years old, from Rugao, a coachman at the Shunda Carriage Company across from Laian Lane on Xinmin Road. They fought each other. Du, being weaker, kicked wildly, causing Lu to be kicked in the kidney. Lu immediately clutched his testicles and cried for help. His family took him to Lu's mistress's house at No. 233 Feilun Road, where he died at 8:00 PM that night. His family reported the incident to the Second Branch of the Fifth District, and Du was arrested. Yesterday, the local police chief, Yan Liugen, and the local court were ordered to report the autopsy.

Pirate Zheng Ming Executed by Firing Squad in Changshu

A Cheapened Prison Sentence

Zheng Ming, a famous pirate from Changshu, repeatedly committed serious crimes of kidnapping, extortion, murder, and arson in his hometown. He fled to Shanghai, where he committed robbery and was arrested by the police and handed over to the Special District Court. After the Changshu County Government learned of this, it sent a letter to the Special District Court, approving his extradition to Changshu for trial. If Zheng's crime did not warrant the death penalty, he would still have to be sent back to serve his prison sentence. It is now learned that after Zheng was brought to Changshu, he confessed clearly during interrogation and was sentenced to death. After reporting to the superior for approval, he was executed by firing squad the day before yesterday. The Special District Court has already been officially notified for record.

Car Crashes into Rickshaw on Zhongxing Road

Rickshaw Puller and Passenger Injured

At around 10:00 AM yesterday, at the Nanlu Fanzili intersection on Zhongxing Road, Zhabei, a Huashang Public Bus Company bus with license plate Hua Zhao 4543 and Concession license plate 17905, traveling from Baoshan Road to Zhenru, collided with a rickshaw with Public Works Bureau license plate 1922, pulled by Su Jinlou from Yancheng, coming from the opposite direction. Unable to avoid each other, the rickshaw was overturned. The rickshaw passenger, Zhou Zuzhang from Jiangwan, was on his way to report his grandson's death to his son, who was studying at a university. He was unfortunately injured in the head, bleeding profusely. The rickshaw puller also suffered injuries to his waist, abdomen, arms, and legs. The patrolman Li Qingyin and others from the Zhongxing Road police station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau reported the incident to patrol leaders Chen Ruichun and Cheng Jun, who went to arrest the bus driver Cui Jinsheng and sent the injured Zhou Zuzhang and Su Jinlou to the Fourth District. District Chief Zhou immediately ordered police officer Gao Xinyi to transfer the injured to Baolong Hospital for treatment, where they were bandaged and returned. It is reported that the injuries were not serious. However, the rickshaw was completely crushed and was also sent to the district office for disposal.

Kidnapping Case Discovered in Hotel

Wu Ma Lures Cousin

Detectives Arrest Police Officer

Xu Zhaoying from Nanjing used to run a beef shop in the capital. His wife, Li, 20 years old, is beautiful. Her cousin, Wu Ma, 33 years old, from Pudong, runs a teahouse in Lan Nidou, Pudong. Although Ma is middle-aged, she is exceptionally flirtatious and used to be a matchmaker. She is indeed a busybody. On the 8th of this month, she went to Beijing to visit the Xu family. Xu treated her with great courtesy due to their family relationship. However, seeing that Li was young and beautiful, Ma had impure thoughts and persuaded Li to go to Shanghai, saying how prosperous it was and that she could guide her there, making her forget to return. Li was bewitched and excited to travel. She asked Ma to accompany her to Shanghai. Ma agreed readily, and they came to Shanghai on the 10th. After arriving, Wu Ma took Li to a room in the Central Hotel outside Xiaochemen, Nanshi, for temporary lodging. Soon, Ma went out on the pretext of something. Before long, she suddenly came back with a police officer Hu from the Third District of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. Upon entering the room and seeing Li, Hu smiled brightly, approached and sat on Li's bed, chatting with her. Because Li knew that Hu was acquainted with Ma, she simply gave polite replies. Unexpectedly, Hu suddenly made various indecent gestures. Li realized that something was wrong and intended to resist, fearing that she would be treated harshly. She was immediately terrified and ran out of the room, begging the hotel waiter to drive Hu away. However, the waiter refused firmly. In desperation, Li kowtowed to the waiter repeatedly, begging him to help. The waiter, seeing her pitiful state, went into the room to inquire. At that time, all the guests in the hotel had heard the noise and gathered to watch. Coincidentally, Dong Mingde, the leader of the detective team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and others were going to the hotel to inspect the rooms. Upon learning of the situation, they took everyone back for questioning.

Nothing Gained ·· One Thief Arrested

At the Shengxian Temple Guandi Temple located at 1460 (now changed to 86 and a half) Avenue Edward VII, last night around ten o'clock, the temple was performing a sutra recitation and repentance ceremony for the Du family when suddenly seven robbers arrived. British Public Bus Workers' Petition Yesterday

Demanding Full Reinstatement

The Social Affairs Bureau Will Mediate

Following the resumption of the strike by British public bus workers, the company refused unconditional reinstatement, leading to an impasse. Yesterday, the company continued to operate with ticket inspectors and new employees filling the ticket sales positions, barely managing to run routes 2, 5, 9, and 10. The routes were shortened, and buses returned to the depot early. A uniform fare was charged. After a split within the strike committee, all the workers petitioned the authorities yesterday. The details of yesterday's events are recorded below:

▲ Collective Petition Over one hundred and fifty British public bus striking ticket sellers, including Hong Mingdao, Wu Weixin, Qin Shenchong, Xu Mingfei, etc., all wearing yellow uniforms, went to the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau on Zhonghua Road at one o'clock in the afternoon yesterday to petition for (1) the reinstatement of all ticket sellers, and (2) the company's acceptance of the ten conditions for improved treatment proposed by the workers. The bureau chief, Pan Gongzhan, dispatched a staff member of the Third Section, Bing, to explain the situation to all the workers and accept their demands, promising to find a way to mediate. During the explanation, some workers, feeling oppressed by imperialism, which led to the prolongation of the strike, tearfully pleaded for immediate assistance for the sake of their livelihoods.

▲ Mediation in Progress After the ticket sellers went on strike on August 20 to demand improved treatment, the strike committee sent representatives to the company repeatedly for negotiations, but they were rejected each time. As a result, on August 31, they unconditionally resumed work. However, the company reduced the wages of the reinstated workers to 20 yuan uniformly and fired a large number of workers, forcing them to resume the strike on the 2nd. To this day, the issue remains unresolved, and the workers' livelihoods are unsustainable. In light of this, the Social Affairs Bureau, after receiving the workers' petition yesterday, will consult with the Municipal Party Headquarters to discuss solutions and send representatives to mediate with the company.

Letters to the Editor

Inquiry from Mr. Lin Disheng

Unfortunately, I lost the opportunity to study from a young age. At the age of fourteen, I entered the business world as an apprentice. After years of hard work, I was fortunate enough to obtain a higher position. However, my current knowledge of Chinese language is insufficient for my job. I once heard people say that the only way to improve one's command of Chinese is to read and see a lot. I have followed this advice for several years, reading no less than a hundred books, but the results have been limited. Therefore, I cannot help but doubt the claim that simply reading a lot can improve one's knowledge of Chinese. I respectfully request your guidance on the following two points: (1) Which books did you read when you were studying Chinese, and which books helped you improve your writing skills? (2) What must I do to make significant progress in Chinese?

(Reply) Chinese language has two aspects: (1) thought. Reading more books, reading more newspapers, and observing world events and all human affairs, accumulating rich knowledge, will naturally make your writing respectable, with a clear and correct purpose. This is what is meant by "writing to convey the Dao." (2) Art. Having thoughts requires the ability to express them, which can be divided into two levels: (1) practical writing, which focuses on meeting the needs of the reader by providing what they need. (2) Beautiful writing. It is not easy to say what is beautiful, but a common standard can be stated: it moves the reader. The higher the degree of emotion, the more beautiful. The wider the scope of emotion, the more beautiful. The longer the duration of emotion, the more beautiful.

As for which books to read to improve your Chinese, it is impossible to say.

Inquiry from Mr. Wang Canyi

I am a small clerk in a rice shop, barely making a living with the sweat of my brow. It is already lucky enough that I can secure my own livelihood, let alone support my parents, wear silk, and eat delicacies. In recent days, my parents have been trying to arrange a marriage for me. They have taken all the necessary steps for their son. However, I am constrained by a poor environment, and my parents are already like candles in the wind. At that time, an inexperienced and weak-willed person like me will immediately experience economic panic and may become a beggar. If I tell them this, I am afraid of hurting my parents' feelings, which is something a child should never do. If I comply, I see this yoke being placed on me, leaving me in a dilemma. I sincerely ask the reporter to provide me with a good method to cope with this situation. Please reply in the newspaper. I wish your newspaper a bright future.

(Reply) You are concerned about your economic situation and do not agree with your parents arranging a marriage for you so early, lest your economic situation become even more panicked in the future. Your idea is very good. Moreover, according to the age you mentioned in your letter, you are only eighteen years old, so you can delay it for a few years. You should convey this idea to your parents very sincerely and gently, repeatedly, without offending them. But you must firmly stick to your own opinion.

Inquiry from Mr. Hu Liangcun

Yixian County has little land and many mountains (the mountains are rich in fertile soil and can be cultivated, but the people of the county are biased in their views, emphasizing commerce and despising agriculture and industry, and do not cultivate the land, so that people from other places are now opening up wasteland and making profits). The production is not abundant, the transportation is blocked, and the people's livelihood is difficult. Men go out to do business, and women stay at home to farm and weave, which has become a custom for hundreds of years. In recent years, due to frequent troubles, commerce has been greatly affected, resulting in many unemployed people. People are floating around, wandering on divergent paths. I dare to hope that you will provide guidance on the direction to take in order to make progress.

(Reply) Yixian County has many mountains and little land, and agricultural production is not abundant. The customs emphasize commerce and despise agriculture and industry, causing fertile and suitable mountains to be taken over by people from other places. Since you care about your hometown, you should unite with intellectuals and loudly appeal to the elders of your hometown, advocating "sacred agriculture and industry" and correcting the class concepts that have become a custom. This seems to be a fundamental remedy.

In addition to farming and weaving, women in Yixian County can also engage in some home occupations, such as sewing and raising chickens. Because transportation in Yixian County is blocked, it is inconvenient to go to towns. If they learn to sew and weave cloth, they can make their own clothes, which not only saves expensive tailoring costs but also avoids the trouble of traveling long distances, which can be said to be a win-win situation. The use of eggs is very widespread in the counties of Huizhou. At the end of the year, weddings and happy events, and ordinary people's interactions with guests, all use this to treat guests. The supply cannot meet the demand and relies on other provinces, so the price is very high. If Yixian promotes chicken farming and transports the eggs to Xiuning and other places, it will definitely sell well. As for the feed for chickens, it does not necessarily require grains. It is said that there is a kind of fat insect that is best for feeding chickens. You may want to pay attention to books on chicken farming and guide the people of Yixian County with the best methods. What do you think?

Postal stamp on letters to editor

Treatment Conditions in the Printing Industry Resolved

Two Yuan Salary Increase for All, Establishment of a Children's School

But the Issue of Working Hours is Submitted to Arbitration

The printing industry in this city had announced a shutdown due to workers proposing treatment conditions and voluntarily implementing an eight-hour workday. Later, the Social Affairs Bureau strictly ordered the maintenance of a nine-hour workday before resuming operations. The treatment conditions were repeatedly mediated by the bureau, and both parties were close to an agreement, but the working hours were insisted upon by each side, making it impossible to resolve. The union and the trade association had convened a general meeting to discuss the issue. The workers conceded to eight and a half hours, while the management insisted on nine hours. Yesterday was another day for mediation. The treatment conditions were signed and resolved, but the issue of working hours was declared unresolved. The details of the situation are recorded below:

▲ Authorities Mediate The Social Affairs Bureau convened the Mediation Committee again at one o'clock in the afternoon yesterday to conduct mediation. Dai Zhongxuan and Chen Bingxi, representatives of the trade association, and Wang Xingquan and Xia Hailin, representatives of the printing workers' union, attended. The chairman was Wang Bing of the Social Affairs Bureau, and the recorder was Zhang Gongmu. Regarding the issue of working hours, the management insisted on nine hours based on the wishes of the industry, while the labor side conceded to eight and a half hours based on the wishes of all the workers. The chairman proposed a compromise of eight hours and forty-five minutes, but the management insisted on the original proposal, making it impossible to resolve. The chairman then declared the issue of working hours unresolved and submitted it to arbitration. The remaining conditions, such as increasing wages and food and lodging expenses, were signed by both parties and declared resolved.

▲ Treatment Conditions The original text of the labor-management treatment conditions in the printing industry is as follows: (1) The union and the trade association have the right to represent all their members. (2) When hiring workers, the management must give priority to union members. For union members in this industry, the union must first submit a request to the government for review and approval and open a list to the trade association for selection. (3) Working hours (pending arbitration by the municipal government). (4) The wages of each employee shall be increased by two yuan per month. (5) The management shall subsidize each worker with seven yuan per month for food expenses and two yuan per month for lodging expenses, to be paid in the middle of the month. (6) Sundays and the anniversary of the establishment of the printing industry trade union (March 28) should each be a day of rest. There shall be six days of vacation for the Gregorian New Year. All national holidays and other days temporarily designated by the National Government shall be days of rest, with wages paid as usual. If the management wants to work, the wages shall be doubled. (7) If a worker is sick during his service, the wages shall be paid as usual for a maximum of two months. The management shall bear 60% of the medical expenses, based on the prescription (this does not apply to venereal diseases and lung diseases). In the event of work-related injuries, deaths, or disabilities, the government's laws and regulations shall apply. (8) Workers who have worked for more than eight months shall be given a double salary at the end of the year. Those who have worked in the store for four months shall be given half. If the management's business is sluggish and is indeed losing money, it may be reduced by half after investigation by both labor and management. (9) If a worker encounters marriage (personal) or bereavement (parents and wife), he shall be given leave: three weeks for outside the city and ten days for in the city, with wages paid as usual, and may pre-draw one month's salary. If the stipulated date is exceeded, wages shall not be paid. (10) If the union holds an emergency meeting that has been approved by the party and government agencies, each factory worker shall send representatives to attend, limited to four hours, with wages paid as usual. However, the union must provide a notice of proof. The number of participants shall be one person for every ten people, two people for every twenty people, and so on, but the maximum shall not exceed five people. (11) Workers who are late by no more than 30 minutes per month shall be given one day's wages. Workers who are late six times per month (the total time shall not exceed one and a half hours in the morning) shall have their wages deducted accordingly. (12) The trade association shall establish a school for the children of printing workers within three months. (13) The management shall not dismiss workers without reason. If they are dismissed for reasons other than gross negligence, the union shall be notified in advance. If the business is sluggish or there are special circumstances, the competent authorities shall be reported to first and handled in accordance with the law. (14) Wages shall be paid at least twice a month according to the Gregorian calendar. (15) Abolish all contracting and short-term labor systems. (16) Apprentices shall be given a monthly allowance of one yuan in the first year, two yuan in the second year, and at least seven yuan per month in the third year. (17) Apprentices shall not be assigned factory affairs or dangerous and important work. (18) During the apprenticeship period, apprentices have the obligation to serve the management's vocational instructors faithfully and diligently. The union shall not interfere beyond its authority. (19) After this agreement is concluded, both parties must abide by it and not enter into any private agreements that conflict with this agreement. All original private agreements that conflict with this agreement shall be invalid.

Relief Organizations Should Be Supervised by the Social Affairs Bureau

To Prevent Fundraising Under False Pretenses

A joint public notice from the Municipal Social Affairs and Public Security Bureaus states: "Regarding the joint public notice, we have received Municipal Government Order No. 9584, which states, 'This year's floods and inundations have caused extraordinarily severe disasters. Soliciting donations to rescue the victims is an urgent matter. However, it has been reported that there have been cases of defrauding donations under the guise of disaster relief, which is extremely hateful. After investigation, matters related to temporary relief in this city and the establishment of charitable organizations should be subject to the supervision of the Social Affairs Bureau. Any fundraising activities conducted without prior reporting and registration should be banned to prevent abuses and promote good deeds. In addition to issuing a public notice that all organizations established in this city for the purpose of raising funds for disaster relief must first report and obtain approval for registration to show seriousness, any unauthorized fundraising activities should be strictly banned, and orders should be issued accordingly. Please comply with this order and conduct strict investigations. This is the order.' Based on this, since the floods in various provinces this year, disaster relief organizations in this city have sprung up like mushrooms. In addition, various social organizations and business organizations have launched fundraising activities for disaster relief. While the majority are sincerely charitable and eager to help, it is inevitable that some are raising money under false pretenses. In the future, whether it is a disaster relief organization, a shop, or an individual, if they aim to raise funds for disaster relief, they must first report to this Social Affairs Bureau for approval and registration, and the donation books should be sent for stamping. They must also submit a separate report on income and expenditure afterwards. Those who do not comply with this order will be banned. Due to the previous order, in addition to conducting strict inspections at any time, a joint public notice is hereby issued to inform all citizens. This is the notice. September 12, 20th year of the Republic of China, Public Security Bureau Chief Chen Xizeng, Social Affairs Bureau Chief Pan Gongzhan."

Record of Overseas Chinese Businessmen Returning from Honolulu

A group of six overseas Chinese businessmen from Honolulu, including Lin Xiang, returned to China to visit various ports. They arrived in Shanghai yesterday. Mr. Lin and others are all from Guangdong and have been doing business in Honolulu for many years. Some have not returned to China for more than ten years, and some for eight or nine years. They do not know much about the current situation in their homeland, so before leaving Honolulu, they obtained letters of introduction from the Chinese Consulate to facilitate their business contacts when they return to visit industries in various ports. They also plan to visit Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum in Nanjing and other scenic spots in the capital before returning to Guangdong. They will return to the United States in a month. According to Mr. Lin, speaking to a reporter from the National News Agency, there are 120,000 overseas Chinese in Honolulu who are engaged in commerce and industry. The current situation is not bad, and there is a prosperous atmosphere. Six months ago, they were shrouded in the global recession, and commerce and industry were hit hard. This was not only true for overseas Chinese but also for overseas merchants from other countries, such as Italy, England, France, etc. The Chinese banks that have been established for more than ten years, Huamei and Gonghe, have a good reputation and are trusted by overseas Chinese. The trust companies, Lianhe and Honolulu, have a considerable reputation. The situation of overseas Chinese in Honolulu is more free than those residing in the United States. The government treats Chinese people the same as residents of other countries, so overseas Chinese in Honolulu can raise funds to establish any business that is needed in the local area. Mr. Lin's son, named Bei Jue, is good at Western boxing. At the age of seventeen, he engaged in friendly sparring with foreigners in Honolulu and always won. In October 1930, he participated in the International Games held on the island and competed with athletes from England, Italy, Japan, and the United States. The athletes were no match for him. The judges on the scene praised Mr. Lin's son as a prodigy. After the closing ceremony, he was awarded two gold medals and two gold watches. Mr. Lin cherishes them very much and carries them with him, telling everyone about them.

Soviet Russian Kerosene to be Shipped to China

Considerable Contact Has Been Made

The Shanghai Times reported that the manager of the Soviet Russian Kerosene Trust in Shanghai is currently in contact with major kerosene merchants in this port to sell kerosene, and a contract may be signed soon. There are currently two oil tankers loaded with 2.5 million gallons anchored in Vladivostok, awaiting orders to come south. It is claimed that the Trust only intends to sell 1.5 million gallons per month in China, but it is believed that this is only a vanguard to open up the market. Once it has a stable foothold, it will ship lubricating oil and other refined products in a continuous stream. However, it remains to be seen whether the kerosene market in this port will experience a temporary price war or whether the various companies can still proceed peacefully. It all depends on the nature of the underwriting. It is claimed that for the sake of competitive protection, the Russian side will allow the underwriter in Shanghai to sell kerosene and gasoline at a price that is one cent per gallon lower than that of other companies, regardless of how the market price falls. The Soviet Russian Kerosene Trust established a management office in Shanghai in August. Its manager in Shanghai, Li Banov, has repeatedly contacted oil merchants. He initially intended to find a distributor, who would be controlled by the Trust in sales, but this did not materialize. Later, he tried to persuade capitalists in this port to organize a new organization to establish their own oil pools and packing factories to exclusively sell Russian oil, but this also failed. Now, they only seek to find a wholesale buyer. Therefore, they are exclusively in contact with the Guanghua Kerosene Company. The company is the largest among the oil companies established by Chinese merchants and is the only independent oil company in central and northern China. It has its own oil pools and packing factories. Yesterday, we interviewed its director, Mr. Yu. He claimed that if a satisfactory solution can be negotiated, the company will purchase and sell Russian oil. The company can easily sell the 1.5 million gallons per month without disrupting the market or causing a price war, because at that time, it will stop purchasing American kerosene and replace it with Russian oil. After investigation, China sells about 20 million gallons per month, so 1.5 million gallons is a very small number, and there will be no dumping. The company has already purchased Russian oil in small quantities in the past few months. In the future, after the contract is signed with the Russian side, this kerosene will be transported directly from the ports of the Black Sea, covering almost half the circumference of the earth. However, due to the limited number of oil tankers on the Siberian Railway, it must be transported entirely by sea. Later, the reporter visited the manager of the Soviet Russian Trust in Shanghai, and he claimed that he had gone to Vladivostok to report on the negotiations in Shanghai and asked the person in charge to approve the contract he had signed with Guanghua.

Man Crushed to Death by Jinghu Train

The Jinghu train, which arrived in Shanghai from Beijing the day before yesterday, unexpectedly had a man fall under it at the Zhenru station. His head was crushed by the train wheels, and he was thrown to the side of the road. He was discovered by the railway police, who sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment, but he died yesterday. The two railway police departments have ordered Ji Yitu, the local bailiff, to report the incident to the local court for investigation.

English Little Books For Sale

Only Ten Cents Per Book

Yang Bingxun, the inventor of Bingxun Shorthand, and Qu Chongfu, the inventor of the Qu Telegraph Code, recognizing that the price of gold is extraordinarily high and students find it difficult to buy English books, have specially organized the Tiny Bookstore to sell English little books and abridged English versions of famous European and American authors. Their nature is similar to the current Blue Books series published in America. The difference is that each page has explanations of new words at the bottom, which can help students study on their own. The price of each book, regardless of thickness, is generously set at 30 cents in silver. This is good news for students everywhere who are trying to solve the problem of English textbooks in this time of expensive gold and cheap silver. The store's business office is located at No. 1340 Sichuan Road, Shanghai. Published titles include Aesop's Fables, A Tale of Two Cities, Arabian Nights, a Chinese-English Dictionary, Grammar, etc. The printing is excellent, and the annotations are accurate. To promote these books, schools everywhere are welcome to send letters to purchase samples. Enclose six cents for postage, and they will be sent immediately.

Record of the Meeting at the Jinting Association

The Jinting Association of Dongting Xishan was previously managed by a temporary executive committee organized by fellow villagers in Shanghai, handling all matters related to the association. On the 6th of this month, all fellow villagers in Shanghai held a general meeting at the association to re-elect the directors of the association. As a result of the election, Xu Huimin, Wang Cunxian, Ling Yongxiang, and 12 others were elected as official directors. The new directors held a discussion meeting on the 9th and decided to publicly recommend Wang Cunxian and four other directors to take over the association on the 13th of this month. A ceremony for the new directors to take office will be held on the afternoon of the 20th at 2:00 PM. The Municipal Party Department and the Bureau of Social Affairs will be notified, and various organizations and newspaper offices will be invited to attend and provide guidance. Yesterday, due to rumors of the impending opening of Dongba, the association held a temporary emergency meeting. After discussion by the directors present, the following resolutions were made: (1) A telegram will be sent to the provincial government urging them to promptly prevent the opening of Dongba to protect the lives of the people. (2) It is rumored that unscrupulous merchants are hoarding and suppressing the market price of autumn silkworm cocoons in Xishan. A telegram will be sent to the Wu County government to thoroughly investigate. (3) Directors Jin Yongqing and Hu Ziyi will be publicly recommended to request Mao Leng to allocate a donation of 1,500 silver dollars for Xishan flood relief. Donation books will be printed and distributed to solicit donations. (4) After the directors take office, they will handle affairs impartially and with absolute transparency to promote the development of the association.

Advantages of the Shunfeng Brand New Car

Since the Madi Automobile Company at No. 10 Edward Road displayed the new Shunfeng brand car the day before yesterday, people from all walks of life have been vying to visit and admire the car's engineering innovations, its stability resembling an eight-cylinder car despite being a four-cylinder car, and its four-cylinder car economy. It is said to be a rare masterpiece in the automotive field and sufficient to open a new era for four-cylinder cars. The car is priced low and has a total of eight styles. The characteristics it possesses are too numerous to mention, the most notable being its natural buoyancy, free-eating gears, easy and safe power transmission, and double-drop frame, etc. The natural buoyancy is especially a standout feature, as the vibration of a four-cylinder engine is a unique flaw that engineering experts have been unable to solve. Now that the invention of natural buoyancy has been successful, all vibrations are completely avoided. In addition to these major features, the Shunfeng brand new car also has many other advantages, such as beautiful lines, harmonious colors, and exquisite decoration and equipment. With such an inexpensive and beautiful car, its future sales success can be predicted.

Free Talk

Random Jottings from the Buchen Zhai Studio

Viewing Jingwei and Zhimo's Happy Event

Two days after the Mid-Autumn Festival in the 14th year of the Republic [1925], Xu Zhimo invited us to Haining to watch the tide. Those who went with us included Chen Weizhe, Hu Shih, Zhu Jingnong, Wang Jingwei, Ren Shuyong, an American female professor, and other people I can't remember. Someone asked Jingnong, "What makes you so happy?" Jingwei said, "Getting married? You have to treat us to a wedding feast." I said, "Better than getting married." Jingwei said, "Then it's having a son." Zhimo said, "Having a son is not as good as getting married; getting married is not as good as getting engaged; getting engaged is not as good as proposing; proposing is not as good as not getting proposed to." In these few words, we can find two kinds of worldviews. Jingwei's guess is the psychology of ordinary Chinese people; Zhimo's words are the attitude of a poet. The psychology of ordinary Chinese people is to ask for more fortune, longevity, and sons. Getting married is joyous; having a son is even more joyous. But the poet's view is different. Only when you lose love can you write good poetry. Goethe lost Charlotte, and The Sorrows of Young Werther occupied the hearts of young people all over the world. Zhimo knew this truth but could not follow it for life. After Xiaoman said "Yes," the muse of poetry said goodbye to Zhimo without saying goodbye. Of course, he would still write poetry, but it was not as good as before. In the eyes of people who love to read Zhimo's poetry, this is such a great loss!

A Record of Two Eccentrics in Tokyo

— Lao Qu

In Tokyo, Japan, every day at sunset, two people who look like beggars can often be seen wandering near the tram station. One is about 40 years old, and the other will soon be 40 years old. The raggedness of their clothes is even worse than that of beggars. They pick up discarded items on the ground, such as cigarette butts and scraps of cloth, and put them all in their bags. Their daily diet often depends on the leftovers of wealthy families. Therefore, every mealtime, they stop near the corners of the walls of wealthy families. When they see discarded food, they rush forward to ask for it and chew it very sweetly, as if there is still an aftertaste. One of these two people is named Satake Otohiki, and the other is named Hibun-ya Kazuichi. At first glance, they would be mistaken for people from the Hindenin [leper colony], but in reality, these two people live in Hibusamachi, Tokyo. Although they are not enormously wealthy, they have tens of thousands of assets. The reason why they are like this is that they are inherently stingy and do not want to spend a penny on food and clothing. Therefore, everyone regards them as eccentric.

When Satake was in his twenties, he and Hibun were both tram conductors, traveling between Yokohama and Kobe. What the Japanese call a "conductor" is the person who drives the train. The two of them are stingy by nature and share the same aspirations. Not only are their clothes torn and dirty, but apart from the uniforms given by the company, they do not even have undershirts. All their wages are saved. Later, the company felt that the character of Satake and Hibun was too low and ordered them to be dismissed. From then on, the two of them lived their beggar's life and never sought employment again. Every day, they put the money they begged into the bank for savings. All their clothes and food are obtained by begging, so they can spend nothing all day long. This has been going on for twenty years.

It has been found that Satake owns three city houses in Tokyo and has savings of 13,000 yuan in the bank. The most peculiar thing is that he has the rights to 24 telephone lines, which he rents out to others and collects rent. Tokyo telephones are often more in demand than supply. Therefore, getting a telephone is considered very difficult. There are often people who pay 2,000 to 3,000 yuan in gold to acquire a telephone. Therefore, it is also one of their assets. It is not known how they were able to obtain the rights to these 24 telephone lines. Each telephone earns a monthly rent of 6 yuan. These 24 telephones already bring in 144 yuan each month. In total, their monthly income is over 400 yuan. After Satake receives the money, he immediately deposits it into the bank and never touches a penny of it. Hibun seems to be slightly inferior to Satake. He owns two city houses in Tokyo, has savings of over 11,000 yuan in the bank, and owns 17 telephones, bringing in over 300 yuan each month. However, Hibun still lives his beggar's life, with the same goals as Satake. Therefore, everyone in Tokyo calls them two monsters.

Appeal for Fellow Gamblers to Contribute a Portion of Their Winnings to Clothing Relief

— Zhizhong

Since the water disaster is serious, what we hear and see in Shanghai is nothing but appeals for disaster relief. It can also be seen that people are willing to share their clothing and food and have compassion. Yesterday, at a friend's house, I saw an appeal for contributing a portion of gambling taxes to clothing relief. Its language is elegant and it is a new approach in disaster relief. I am rushing to reveal it as follows:

Calling "pheasant" [a gambling term] and calling "Lu" [another gambling term], life is about having fun. Without clothes or rags, how can the common people survive the year? Gambling with arrows for 3,000 coins is originally a tool for seeking pleasure, but taking one-tenth of the winnings is certainly a resource for disaster relief. Having seen the great floods reaching the sky and the starving people everywhere, even if the lucky ones escape drowning, they cannot withstand the bitter cold. Seeing Zheng Xia's picture of displaced people, how can we bear to let a single person not be clothed? Imitating Bao Shu's distribution of gold, why not use the five woods [dice] as a connection? Fellow gamblers, spending their days leisurely and playing games, are certainly not making isolated bets. How can we rely on pig herders and slaves? Collecting taxes is a long-term plan, and we must rely on wealthy gamblers. There must be someone in charge of this matter. Why not take advantage of this opportunity, divide the surplus in small amounts, and gather contributions to make a fur coat? Extend compassion to our compatriots, and taking off our clothes is truly an act of kindness. Pity these survivors and call them all to come. If we extract five out of ten, we can accumulate thousands out of tens of thousands. Of course, we are only asking for a portion of the winnings. Please do not resent the request to "distribute the sprouts." Don't laugh at working for others, and we will certainly repay you. This is the appeal.

The Tragic Robbery of One Word and Five Lives

— Jing Mengdie

Night in a High Building

— Kai

Recently, bandits have been restless, and looting is often heard. Small, well-off families in the countryside now have sleepless nights. Yesterday, a friend from the countryside came to Xishan and told me about a most tragic robbery case. It happened a few days ago, a little over ten miles from my home, in the area where Danyang and Wujin meet. There is a village called Maojiatang. A resident, Old Man Chen, originally from Jiangbei, moved here many years ago and became wealthy through hard work. Now he is old and his children and grandchildren surround his knees. He is content with his later years. A certain Jia in the village borrowed 10,000 tiles from Old Man Chen to build a house in early spring, and he did not return them for a long time. Old Man Chen repeatedly asked him to return them. Recently, they met in a teahouse in a nearby village, and they brought up the old matter again. Jia told Old Man Chen, "I will return 5,000 tomorrow, and the remaining 5,000, please wait until next year, okay?" Old Man Chen nodded in agreement. Unexpectedly, someone eavesdropping nearby mistakenly thought it was 5,000 silver dollars. The next night, a group of thieves broke into the house. When they saw Old Man Chen, they immediately asked him for 5,000 silver dollars. In reality, Old Man Chen's family had no cash at all. All they had were grains, which had not been sold because the market price was not good. The thieves, finding nothing, set the house on fire to vent their anger, burning to death two sons and two daughters in the house, all grandchildren of Old Man Chen. Furthermore, the eldest grandson who went out to sound the gong was killed by a gunshot. After he fell to the ground, the sound of the gong still rang, so they added several more shots. At dawn, Old Man Chen, seeing the tragic scene of his family's destruction, cried out and died. Alas, a mistake in words brought disaster to the whole family. The cause of the fire seemed to be the trickery of ghosts and gods. However, Old Man Chen was kind and weak. He always took the lead in contributing to local public welfare and good deeds. He truly did not contend with the world or bear grudges against anyone. He was not like a local tyrant. And what he encountered was so tragic. Could it be that his fate was predetermined? Living to this point, what is the meaning of heaven's justice? I say the same about Old Man Chen's affair.

Song Bowls

— Li Shuping

A friend came from Hunan and told me about the discovery of ancient Song Dynasty bowls in Hunan Province, which is quite peculiar. I am recording it with my pen to inform the people of the country.

Hunan Province has been vigorously constructing highways in recent years. In order to fill and build roads, they have been excavating mountain walls in a certain village on the south road of Xiangtan County. A road worker, a certain Jia, was digging a mountain cave and discovered six magnetic bowls. They were about seven inches in diameter and three inches high. The outside of the bowls was covered with sticky mud. After he took them home and washed them clean, they were radiant with five colors, glittering and dazzling. The road worker placed them in his home and did not think much of it. After a long time, someone told a certain engineer of the road bureau that they were not ordinary items. The engineer knew that a certain Westerner was skilled at appreciation, so he borrowed them to take a look. The Westerner held them up one by one for inspection. Although there was no date to examine, the colors were elegant, the texture was light, and when struck, the sound was clear and far-reaching. Therefore, he determined that they were relics from the Song Dynasty, made of combined pearls and jade, which is why they could be dazzling and last for a long time without changing. He then asked how much they were worth. The road worker raised both hands together and shook them, meaning that the price was not worth mentioning. However, the Westerner mistakenly thought he was asking for ten thousand. The road worker was a local villager who was used to using cash and did not know what a check was. He left it on the table and ignored it, and handed the bowls to the Westerner to take away. When the engineer left, he told him that the check was worth ten thousand and should be carefully preserved. The road worker did not believe him and laughed, "If this paper is really worth ten thousand, please divide it equally with me." The engineer happily agreed and put the check in his pocket, saying, "I will go to Hankou to the bank to cash it for you." He then left with the Westerner. In less than a month, he indeed sent back 5,000 silver dollars. The road worker was caught off guard and suddenly became a wealthy man, and was indescribably happy. The engineer has since resigned from his position and taken the money to study in a certain country. The Westerner, who obtained these six bowls, disappeared without a trace.

Shuping says that since the Boxer Rebellion, countless treasures from our country have flowed overseas. The Royal Museum in London is mostly filled with old collections from our country. If we were to witness it, there would be no one who would not be heartbroken. These six bowls can also be said to be rare treasures and should be stored in domestic museums or exhibition halls for permanent display. How can we allow foreigners to easily take them away at a low value? The worker was certainly ignorant, but the engineer cannot escape his blame. (Remitting Rewards for Disaster Relief)

Random Musings from the Di Xiang Zhai Studio

— Gan Yi

Zhang Hucheng and Zhou Xuexi

It has been 20 years since the Republic. Those in charge of government finances change every year, or even several times a year. There have always been a few wise men, but there are many who rise to high positions whose talents are not sufficient to meet the requirements. Aside from borrowing money and levying taxes, there is no other way. I admire Zhang Daishan (Hu) and Zhou Jizhi's (Xuexi) way of handling affairs, which was appropriate and measured. Both Hu and Xuexi passed the top-level imperial examinations. One became a supervisory censor, and the other became a prefect. Both had a good reputation during the late Qing Dynasty. Hu was especially rich in literary talent and quick-witted. During the years of Jia-Yin and Yi-Mao [1914-1915], Yuan Shikai held power, and his authority dominated the country. There was a view of embellishing the state. At that time, Xuexi was in charge of the Ministry of Finance, and Hu was the deputy minister also managing the Salt Administration. Xuexi held a policy of increasing revenue and reducing expenditure, which was effective. As a result, the national treasury was not exhausted, and government expenses were sufficient. It was unheard of for generals to forcibly demand military funds. Even powerful figures such as Feng Guozhang and Zhang Xun rarely made unreasonable demands. Qu Yingguang even plundered vast amounts of money to aid the central government. This was certainly due to Yuan Shikai's coercion, but also to the efforts of Xuexi and Hu. After a long time, the two often disagreed on matters. Xuexi was stingy and often unreasonable, while Hu was extravagant and had a reputation for being bold and decisive. It was difficult for them to tolerate each other. Xuexi, relying on Yuan Shikai's favor, revealed Hu's shortcomings in a certain case. It was not known whether Yuan Shikai was aware of the facts. While Xuexi was consulting with him, Yuan Shikai wanted to say something, but he couldn't get the words out. He reluctantly ordered Hu to be dismissed from his position and sent far away to Sichuan. He secretly sent someone to comfort Hu, saying that Liu Yan's management of finances was unsurpassed, and Guan Zhong would eventually be reused. "The fault is with me. It is best to avoid it temporarily." Hu lingered and could not leave. Later, Hu was reinstated and Zhou Ziqi (Ziqi) took over Xuexi's post. Xuexi had already received the news and rushed to pay his respects. Ziqi was already seated. Yuan Shikai waited until Xuexi finished speaking and said angrily, "I knew what kind of person you are. Why don't you understand my interests? Those who handle big matters cannot begrudge small expenses." He looked at Ziqi and said, "Jizhi has worked hard for a long time and should rest. You can replace him. Follow Xiao He's rules, and I will be at ease." Ziqi strongly stated that he did not have the talent or ability to overcome this position. Yuan Shikai said, "Say no more. You will not be forgiven if you say more." Ziqi did not speak again. Xuexi left disappointed and immediately submitted his resignation. After several years, Hu also retired as the Grand Secretary of Finance. In the year of Jiazi [1924], he rose again as the Grand Sima. Xuexi suspected that Hu might not have forgotten the past and would seek revenge. He was uneasy. His father, Yushan (Fu), wrote a letter to Hu, accusing his son of his past mistakes. Hu read the letter and laughed, saying, "As the proverb says, it is difficult for one person to satisfy everyone. Also, 'Life is full of meetings and partings.'" He wrote back to Fu, saying, "During my term, I will not allow these matters to be exposed again." Fu often told people about it, saying, "Daishan is, after all, a scholar and his magnanimity is far-reaching."

The Rotary Society of Storytellers

A Husband's Wife (12)

— Jiang Hongjiao

At the same time, Mr. Chen and his wife's argument had failed. He refused to open his mouth and simply covered himself with the quilt and lay in bed, pretending not to hear whatever his wife said. This attitude was, of course, also a feminine attitude. When Mrs. Chen saw that he was not saying anything, she naturally stopped arguing after a while.

From that day on, these two couples harbored great resentment and a thick wall of separation between them. However, Lan Zhen felt sorry for Mr. Chen being oppressed by his wife, while Mr. Li approved of Mrs. Chen's straightforwardness. Mrs. Chen even went to Mr. Li's office to chat, or went to the movies, to the dance hall, or to friends' houses to play cards. Mr. Li still went home after finishing his official business as usual, but Lan Zhen often went to Mr. Chen's house to chat. What Lan Zhen talked about at first was limited to Mr. Li's absurdity and unfaithfulness. She also told Mr. Chen about waiting for her husband in the snow and seeing a woman in the car. Mr. Chen volunteered to investigate whether this woman was an ordinary prostitute, Mr. Li's mistress, or an unofficial lover. Once he had some clues, he would definitely tell Lan Zhen in detail.

Mr. Chen and Lan Zhen were actually both oppressed, so everyone complained. The more people complain, the easier it is for them to click and get along. They had long opportunities to talk every day, and their friendship gradually deepened. At the same time, Mr. Li and Mrs. Chen naturally became closer in the darkness of movie theaters and dance halls. Mrs. Chen did not manage many things at Mr. Chen's house because she was not often at home, so she asked Mrs. Li to help manage them. Even making the bed, folding the quilt, mending socks, and preparing the evening meals were all managed by Mr. Li. In fact, Mrs. Li was equal to Mr. Chen's wife, and Mr. Li was Mrs. Chen's husband. From the perspective of old morality, what an absurd history this was!

However, Mr. Chen's burden was therefore increased. He felt sorry for Mrs. Li's frugality, so he often gave her some clothes or other things, at least twenty or thirty yuan or so a month.

Mr. Li's burden also increased. It was naturally his responsibility to play with Mrs. Chen outside every day. There was no reason to let the woman bear this expense. The more he spent, the more stingy his family became, and even the daily food expenses were not paid in full.

Commercial News

Financial Gold Bar Continues to Decline

▲Final Cut of Two Taels: Yesterday, the 12th, the gold bar continued its downward trend, with extreme volatility and unstoppable turbulence. Initially, it hovered around 760 taels, stabilizing at noon with a difference of seven taels. Ultimately, it fell by two taels and several qian. Market sentiment among traders remained erratic, with various firms pursuing different strategies. The silver market suddenly surged, opening lower at 57 taels. However, active buying followed, particularly due to the decline in foreign exchange rates. This led to a resurgence, exceeding 60 taels and reaching 63 taels and some change. Next month, the market will be closed on Saturdays. It is rumored that the Bombay exchange plans to reduce the rupee exchange rate from 1.6 to 1.4. If silver standard is restored, should gold prices be suppressed? However, the implementation date remains uncertain. The market conditions this week have been particularly complex, with the highest price reaching 75 taels and two qian, and the lowest at 54 taels, a difference of 21 taels and two qian. Overall, it has continued to fall by seven taels and one qian. The market conditions yesterday are as follows:

▲Sharp Decline at the Opening: The opening price for October delivery fell sharply by more than seven taels and four qian to 758 taels and five. This was because both silver and silver prices rose by one-eighth, and US stocks rose by slightly more than nine jiao. Subsequently, the price fluctuated between 58 and 59.5 taels. Trading activity varied. Then, due to sales by Yongfeng, Fuchang, and the Dalian Gang, the price dropped to 56 taels and eight qian. Suddenly, Hengxing, Yiyu, Shunli, and Wanxing stepped in to buy, and the British gold price initially eased and then stabilized. Zhengjin and others initially bought January 25, and December 3125. Then, Chaoxian (Korean) and Mitsui matched the current month's 1875. The gold price rose steadily, reaching 61 taels and eight qian at 9:20, with slight fluctuations of one or two taels. HSBC's listed price remained unchanged. Senchang and Hengxing sold, bringing the price to 60 taels, immediately rebounding by two taels and two or three qian. Afterward, there were fluctuations of one tael or so. Various firms' transactions differed, but the volume was not large. American Cotton Hedging Sales Increased Slightly Last Week

A telegram report from New York on the 11th reports on the cotton market for a week, saying that the government's cotton production estimate on Tuesday was slightly higher than the public's expectations, but the impact was not significant. The increase in hedging sales for the whole week was very small. President Hoover's discussions with the federal banks and cotton merchants on the establishment of a private bank, credit loans, and the export of American cotton have reduced speculators' sales and aroused temporary purchases, but the price has reversed, and the supply has easily increased. Most experts firmly believe that the reduction in planting movement and other relief raw cotton events in the next season are now holding movements in the South. Although cotton harvest is still delayed, the weather is still good, and the market is quite quiet. The weather is generally wait-and-see. If the harvest progresses, hedging sales are expected to increase.
